No tag-name boundary check, no exclusion list, no exemption for known utility forms (variant tabs, activity builder, etc.). It is not section-aware, not form-name-aware, and not nesting-aware. Any string containing `<form` \u2014 even a button row or a tiny one-button submit \u2014 flips the bypass on.\n\nAnd here is what that flip does (line 993):\n\n```python\nif section >= V2_TOTAL_SECTIONS or _body_has_form:\n    main_block = f\"\"\"\n      ...\n      <div class=\"frol-actions\" style=\"margin-top:18px;\">\n        <div>{back_link}</div>\n        <div></div>             <!-- empty! no Save & Continue button -->\n      </div>\n      ...\n    \"\"\"\nelse:\n    main_block = f\"\"\"\n      ...\n      <form id=\"frol-form\" data-step=\"{section}\" data-version=\"2\" ...>\n        <input type=\"hidden\" name=\"action\"  value=\"advance_v2\">\n        ...\n        <button type=\"submit\" class=\"frol-btn\">{advance_label} &rarr;</button>\n      </form>\n      ...\n    \"\"\"\n```\n\nWhen `_body_has_form` is `True`, the entire outer advance form \u2014 including the `Save & Continue` button \u2014 is **omitted**. The body returned by `render_section_11` **does contain `<form`** \u2014 four occurrences, all from the **variant tab bar** (`/frol-set-variant`, one form per variant button: Weekday / Saturday / Sunday / John traveling).\n2. Because `_body_has_form` is a bare substring match, those four utility forms trip the bypass.\n3. The `_body_has_form` guard was originally written to protect \u00a7\u00a72\u201310 (where the Phase C mount has its own forms, hence the comment about \u00a7\u00a72\u201310 losing their button) and \u00a714 (which had a real nested-form hijack bug). ./.local/state/replit/agent/transcript/45564572-518f-44dc-aa9a-67eebfb01771/transcript.jsonl:{"memory_id": 14552, "messages": [{"role": "assistant", "content": [{"type": "text", "text": "Lauren has **25 targets** in her data \u2192 `not targets` is `False` \u2192 she takes the **main path at line 3879**, not the early-return at line 3743. So the early-return theory is ruled out. Both call sites pass `12` anyway, so even if she were on the empty path, the chrome would be identical.\n\n## 2. `frolAdvance` redirect handling \u2014 verbatim (static/js/frol_wizard.js lines 386\u2013399)\n\n```javascript\nfetch(\"/frol-wizard\", { method: \"POST\", body: fd, credentials: \"same-origin\", redirect: \"manual\" })\n  .then(function (r) {\n    /* opaqueredirect (status 0 with redirect:manual) and 2xx are both success */\n    var ok = r.ok || r.type === \"opaqueredirect\" || r.status === 0;\n    if (!ok) {\n      status(\"Save failed (\" + r.status + \")\");\n      if (btn) { btn.disabled = false; btn.textContent = \"Save & Continue\"; }\n      return;\n    }\n    status(\"Saved\");\n    var next = (parseInt(step, 10) || 0) + 1;\n    var modeQs = mode ? (\"&mode=\" + encodeURIComponent(mode)) : \"\";\n    window.location.href = \"/frol-wizard?step=\" + next + modeQs;\n  })\n```\n\n### Does it read the server's `Location` header?\n\n**No.** With `redirect: \"manual\"`, `fetch` returns an `opaqueredirect` response whose headers (including `Location`) are **inaccessible to JavaScript by design** \u2014 the spec forbids reading them. Even if it tried, `r.headers.get(\"Location\")` would return `null`.\n\n### How does it pick the destination URL?\n\n**It constructs the URL itself**, ignoring whatever the server actually said:\n\n```javascript\nvar next = (parseInt(step, 10) || 0) + 1;\nwindow.location.href = \"/frol-wizard?step=\" + next + modeQs;\n```\n\nWhere `step` is the value passed into `frolAdvance(event, step, mode)` \u2014 which comes from the form's `onsubmit=\"return frolAdvance(event, 12, 'structured')\"` template, populated from the same `section` argument as `_section_chrome`.\n\n## Implication for the \u00a712 \u2192 \u00a713 hop\n\nThe client-side navigation is **completely decoupled from the server's `Location` header**. For Duration Review:\n\n- Form: `onsubmit=\"return frolAdvance(event, 12, 'structured')\"`\n- JS computes: `next = 12 + 1 = 13`\n- Browser navigates to: `/frol-wizard?step=13&mode=structured` \u2192 **Build Your Day** \u2713\n\nThe server's redirect target (also `step=13`) is irrelevant to where the browser actually lands \u2014 but they happen to agree, so this is fine for Duration Review.\n\n## Real risk this design creates (worth flagging, even though it's not the current bug)\n\nBecause the client computes `next = step + 1` instead of trusting the server, **any section whose true \"next\" is not `+1` will silently desynchronise**. Two examples already in the codebase that would be vulnerable:\n\n1. The legacy `/frol-wizard` POST handler at app.py line 7373 has a special branch that redirects to `step=14` from \u00a713 in certain conditions (skipping \u00a713b). The browser would still navigate to `step=14` here by coincidence (13+1=14), but only because the numbers align.\n2. If a future section is ever skipped conditionally (e.g. skip \u00a711 Holidays when no holidays are configured), the server would 302 to step=12 but the client would navigate to step=12 from \u00a711 anyway \u2014 coincidentally correct only for `+1` skips.\n\nThe principled fix would be to either drop `redirect: \"manual\"` (let the browser follow the redirect on its own, which `fetch` does automatically with the default `\"follow\"` mode for POST\u2192302\u2192GET) or to switch to a server-rendered form submit (no fetch at all) so the browser handles the redirect natively. But that's a design call, not a directed fix, so I'm just flagging it.\n\n## Bottom line for the \u00a712 button\n\n- Both `_section_chrome` calls in `render_section_11` pass `12`. \u2713\n- The body in Lauren's case is the full grid (25 targets), not the empty-state. \u2713\n- `frolAdvance` ignores the server `Location` and navigates to `/frol-wizard?step=13&mode=structured`. \u2713 (numerically correct for this hop)\n\nNothing in the \u00a712 path is wrong. If Lauren is still seeing it fail, the failure has to be one of:\n- Cached pre-fix HTML (no `#frol-form`, no button at all)\n- The page she's actually on is not \u00a712 \u2014 Holidays (\u00a711) was the most recent POST per `completed_steps`\n- A 500 from `render_section_12` (Build Your Day) on the GET after the redirect\n\nNone of which would be fixed by editing `render_section_11`'s chrome arguments.\n\nNo changes made."}]}]}

these\n\n1. No backslashes inside f-strings\n2. No nested quotes inside f-strings \u2014 use a variable outside the f-string instead\n3. All POST routing uses elif chains \u2014 never if/elif with a missing first if, never nested if blocks for routing\n4. Never put import statements inside if blocks or functions\n5. All file writes use safe_save_json (tmp file + os.replace) \u2014 never open(f, 'w') directly\n6. No walrus operator (`:=`)\n7. Never use `'\\n'` inside a JS string within a Python string literal \u2014 use `'\\\\n'` so the browser receives the escape sequence, not a raw newline\n8. **multipart/form-data parsing** \u2014 when fetch POSTs use FormData the server receives multipart/form-data not urlencoded. The do_POST handler must sniff Content-Type and parse accordingly using cgi.FieldStorage for multipart. If a POST handler receives empty data check the Content-Type first.\n9. **py_compile passes but runtime fails** \u2014 py_compile only validates syntax not runtime correctness. Always run an in-process smoke test after py_compile to catch NameError, missing variable definitions, and import failures.\n10. **test fixtures must never write to live data** \u2014 verification harnesses must always operate on a temp copy of live data files. Never call save_progress, safe_save_json, or any write helper on live data during testing. Always restore from backup after any test that touches data files.\n11. **double-escaping HTML entities** \u2014 never pass a string that is already HTML-escaped through escape() again. If a string contains literal ampersands for display use plain ampersands in the source string and let escape() handle it once. Strings pre-escaped with `&amp;` will render as visible `&amp;` in the browser if escaped again.\n12. **JS newline in Python f-strings applies everywhere** \u2014 rule 7 applies to ALL files containing JS embedded in Python, not just render_frol_wizard.py. This includes render_schedule.py, render_timeblock.py, render_lucy.py, render_lorenzo.py, and any other render file with inline JavaScript.\n\n### Additional rules (13\u201318)\n\n13. **FROL WIZARD NESTED FORM ADDENDUM** \u2014 The _body_has_form check in _section_chrome looks for `action=\"/frol-wizard\"` in the body string. Any form inside a section body posting to /frol-wizard will suppress the Save and Continue button. Variant tab forms posting to /frol-set-variant are safe. Activity builder forms posting to /frol-add-activity are safe. Before adding any form to a section body confirm its action attribute. This is a recurring bug \u2014 document before fixing if it appears again.\n\n14. **PRE-FLIGHT CHECKLIST** \u2014 Before writing any spec answer these questions. One \u2014 how many files does this touch, list them, if unknown that is a diagnosis step first. Two \u2014 does it involve JavaScript inside Python f-strings, if yes flag the backslash-n rule explicitly in the spec. Three \u2014 does it touch form handling, if yes confirm no nested forms posting to /frol-wizard. Four \u2014 is the root cause confirmed or assumed, if assumed run diagnosis first never draft a fix on an assumed cause. Five \u2014 does it touch multiple files at once, if yes break into separate single-purpose instructions. Six \u2014 does it involve data shape changes or migration, if yes confirm before and after data structure explicitly before writing the spec.\n\n15. **CLAUD.MD READ-BACK REQUIRED** \u2014 At the start of every session read claud.md and paste back every rule found. Then identify which rules apply to today's task. If you cannot paste the rules back accurately stop and ask Lauren to re-paste claud.md before proceeding.\n\n16. **MAGNIFICA HUMANITAS DESIGN PRINCIPLES** \u2014 Every feature built must reflect these principles. One \u2014 the app is a tool not an authority. Every AI suggestion is framed as a suggestion never a prescription. Language uses \"here is one way to think about this\" never \"you should\" or \"the optimal schedule is.\" Two \u2014 companions serve real relationships they do not replace them. Every companion orients toward real people, real community, and real pastoral support. Sister Mary never replaces a confessor. Father Gregory never replaces real mentors. Lucy regularly suggests real conversations over app conversations. Three \u2014 AI supports thinking it does not replace it. Ask before suggesting. Boys build their own plans before seeing AI suggestions. Father Gregory asks questions more than he gives answers. Four \u2014 be transparent about what AI is. Companions never make theological claims with personal authority. Prayer texts come from verified Catholic sources only never AI generated. Five \u2014 language of grace not performance. No gamification no streaks no scores that shame. A hard day is never framed as failure. Sick Day Mode is relief not defeat. Six \u2014 subsidiarity. The family governs itself. Lauren is always the authority. The app serves the family's discernment it does not replace it. Seven \u2014 formation in digital wisdom. Father Gregory teaches the boys to think critically about AI. The explicit goal is that JP finishes high school able to plan his day without the app.\n\n17. **ONE FIX PER INSTRUCTION** \u2014 Never bundle multiple fixes into one Agent instruction unless they are in the same file and directly related. Parser spine, verbatim (`app.py:5806\u20135907`):\n\n```python\n                # \u2500\u2500 Parse [MEAL_UPDATE:Day:slot[|recipe=ID]]meal[/MEAL_UPDATE] and save \u2500\u2500\n                _meal_rx = _re.compile(\n                    r'\\[MEAL_UPDATE:([^:\\]]+):([^|\\]]+)(?:\\|recipe=([^\\]]+))?\\]'\n                    r'([\\s\\S]*?)\\[\\/MEAL_UPDATE\\]',\n                    _re.IGNORECASE\n                )\n                try:\n                    from render_meals import MEAL_SLOT_SET as _DICT_OK_SLOTS\n                except Exception:\n                    _DICT_OK_SLOTS = {\"breakfast\",\"lunch\",\"dinner\",\"dessert\",\"snacks\",\"dad_lunch\"}\n                _meal_updates_found = []\n                for _mm in _meal_rx.finditer(text):\n                    _mday  = _mm.group(1).strip()\n                    _mslot = _mm.group(2).strip().lower()\n                    _mrid  = (_mm.group(3) or \"\").strip()\n                    if _mrid and not _re.fullmatch(r\"[^\\s\\[\\]]+\", _mrid):\n                        print(f\"[lorenzo MEAL_UPDATE] rejected malformed recipe_id: {_mrid!r}\")\n                        _mrid = \"\"\n                    _mmeal = _mm.group(4).strip()\n                    if _mday and _mslot:\n                        _save_ok = False\n                        try:\n                            _wk = _planning_week_key()\n                            _plan = load_meal_plan(_wk)\n                            if _mmeal:\n                                if _mrid and _mslot in _DICT_OK_SLOTS:\n                                    _plan[\"days\"].setdefault(_mday, {})[_mslot] = {\n                                        \"display\":   _mmeal,\n                                        \"recipe_id\": _mrid,\n                                    }\n                                    # [enrichment block elided for length \u2014 app.py:5847\u20135894:\n                                    #  for recipe-linked dinners, fills prep_time/cook_time from\n                                    #  the recipe card, kid 'helpers' via kid_helpers.assign_kid_steps,\n                                    #  and serve_time from the FROL; \"fill blanks only\".]\n                                else:\n                                    _plan[\"days\"].setdefault(_mday, {})[_mslot] = _mmeal\n                            else:\n                                _plan[\"days\"].setdefault(_mday, {}).pop(_mslot, None)\n                            _plan[\"start\"] = _plan.get(\"start\") or _wk\n                            save_meal_plan(_plan)\n                            _save_ok = True\n                        except Exception as _se:\n                            print(f\"[lorenzo MEAL_UPDATE] save failed for {_mday}/{_mslot}: {_se}\")\n                        if _save_ok:\n                            _meal_updates_found.append((_mday, _mslot))\n```\n\n**Where does it write?** To the **`/meal-save-plan` store** \u2014 i.e. the same `data/meal_plan/{Monday}.json`, via the same `save_meal_plan()`. It does **not** write meal data to `planning_session.json` (it only `advance_planning_session()`s the cursor afterward).\n\n**Is it registered in `_JSON_PATHS`?** **No \u2014 and it doesn't need to be, because it never arrives as a POST body.** `_JSON_PATHS = {\"/plan-import-apply\", \"/plan-import-undo-placement\", \"/curriculum-save\", \"/curriculum-minutes\", \"/poetry-passage-save\"}` (`app.py:3453`). The `[MEAL_UPDATE]` text is extracted from the *LLM response*, not from the request body, so the form-parser-consumes-JSON trap (claud.md) cannot apply to it. \n\nWorth noting for completeness: **`/meal-save-plan` is also not in `_JSON_PATHS`, and that is correct** \u2014 it posts `application/x-www-form-urlencoded` fields (`week=\u2026`, `days=<JSON string>`) and `json.loads` the `days` field itself, so the urlencoded parser handles it fine. The claud.md `_JSON_PATHS` gotcha only bites routes that send a **raw JSON request body**; neither save channel does.\n\n---\n\n## Report 4 \u2014 Recommended architecture\n\n**The hypothesis is half-right.** The *store* is already unified \u2014 both `[MEAL_UPDATE]` and `/meal-save-plan` persist to the same `data/meal_plan/{Monday}.json` through `save_meal_plan()`. So the bug is **not** \"two competing stores.\" The real architectural mismatch is in the **save trigger and the confirmation loop**:\n\n1. **The trigger is brittle free-text regex.** `_meal_rx` requires a perfectly-formed `[MEAL_UPDATE:Day:slot]\u2026[/MEAL_UPDATE]`. Any LLM malformation \u2014 missing closing tag, stray bracket/whitespace, the `|recipe=` id failing `[^\\s\\[\\]]+` \u2014 silently yields no match \u2192 **no save**, with no signal back to the model.\n2. **Narration is decoupled from persistence.** Lorenzo's \"I saved it / I couldn't save it\" prose is generated by the model *in the same reply, before the server runs the save*. `_save_ok` captures the *real* result but only feeds `_meal_updates_found` / the false-confirmation guard \u2014 it never corrects the words the model already wrote. Hence \"narrates success or failure inconsistently\": the words and the disk state are produced by two different actors and never reconciled.\n3. **Why the card still renders anyway:** when a tag *is* well-formed, the save genuinely succeeds to the authoritative store, so the fridge card updates \u2014 independent of whatever Lorenzo said.\n\n**Minimum change that would make saves reliable** (recommendation only \u2014 not implemented):\n\n- **Keep the unified store** (`save_meal_plan` / `data/meal_plan/{Monday}.json`) \u2014 don't re-route to `planning_session.json`; that's correct as-is.\n- **Make the confirmation server-driven, not model-driven.** After parsing, the server already knows `_save_ok` and `_meal_updates_found`. The smallest reliable fix is to **stop trusting the model's prose for save status**: strip any model-authored save claims and have the server **append a deterministic confirmation/\u25b2failure line** built from `_save_ok` (e.g. \"Saved Monday dinner \u2713\" / \"Couldn't save Monday dinner \u2014 tag was malformed, try again\"). This closes the narration\u2194persistence gap without changing where data lands.\n- **Optionally tighten the channel** by treating the structured `/meal-save-plan` route as the single write path and having the chat handler *call that same save logic* with parsed args (so there's one persistence code path, one place backups/validation live), rather than a second inline `load\u2192mutate\u2192save` copy. This is a refactor, not required for correctness, but it removes the duplicate save spine.\n\nNet: the fix is **confirmation integrity** (server reports the truth of `_save_ok`), not store migration. The `[MEAL_UPDATE]` channel can stay, but its success/failure messaging must be emitted by the server from the actual save result, not narrated by the model.\n\n---\n\nNo files were modified. I'm skipping the code-review step because this task produced **zero code changes** \u2014 it's a read-only diagnosis deliverable, so there's nothing to review. Tell me which direction you want for the actual fix and I'll scope it as a single change per Rule 17."}]}]}

these\n\n1. No backslashes inside f-strings\n2. No nested quotes inside f-strings \u2014 use a variable outside the f-string instead\n3. All POST routing uses elif chains \u2014 never if/elif with a missing first if, never nested if blocks for routing\n4. Never put import statements inside if blocks or functions\n5. All file writes use safe_save_json (tmp file + os.replace) \u2014 never open(f, 'w') directly\n6. No walrus operator (`:=`)\n7. Never use `'\\n'` inside a JS string within a Python string literal \u2014 use `'\\\\n'` so the browser receives the escape sequence, not a raw newline\n8. **multipart/form-data parsing** \u2014 when fetch POSTs use FormData the server receives multipart/form-data not urlencoded. The do_POST handler must sniff Content-Type and parse accordingly using cgi.FieldStorage for multipart. If a POST handler receives empty data check the Content-Type first.\n9. **py_compile passes but runtime fails** \u2014 py_compile only validates syntax not runtime correctness. Always run an in-process smoke test after py_compile to catch NameError, missing variable definitions, and import failures.\n10. **test fixtures must never write to live data** \u2014 verification harnesses must always operate on a temp copy of live data files. Never call save_progress, safe_save_json, or any write helper on live data during testing. Always restore from backup after any test that touches data files.\n11. **double-escaping HTML entities** \u2014 never pass a string that is already HTML-escaped through escape() again. If a string contains literal ampersands for display use plain ampersands in the source string and let escape() handle it once. Strings pre-escaped with `&amp;` will render as visible `&amp;` in the browser if escaped again.\n12. **JS newline in Python f-strings applies everywhere** \u2014 rule 7 applies to ALL files containing JS embedded in Python, not just render_frol_wizard.py. This includes render_schedule.py, render_timeblock.py, render_lucy.py, render_lorenzo.py, and any other render file with inline JavaScript.\n\n### Additional rules (13\u201318)\n\n13. **FROL WIZARD NESTED FORM ADDENDUM** \u2014 The _body_has_form check in _section_chrome looks for `action=\"/frol-wizard\"` in the body string. Any form inside a section body posting to /frol-wizard will suppress the Save and Continue button. Variant tab forms posting to /frol-set-variant are safe. Activity builder forms posting to /frol-add-activity are safe. Before adding any form to a section body confirm its action attribute. This is a recurring bug \u2014 document before fixing if it appears again.\n\n14. **PRE-FLIGHT CHECKLIST** \u2014 Before writing any spec answer these questions. One \u2014 how many files does this touch, list them, if unknown that is a diagnosis step first. Two \u2014 does it involve JavaScript inside Python f-strings, if yes flag the backslash-n rule explicitly in the spec. Three \u2014 does it touch form handling, if yes confirm no nested forms posting to /frol-wizard. Four \u2014 is the root cause confirmed or assumed, if assumed run diagnosis first never draft a fix on an assumed cause. Five \u2014 does it touch multiple files at once, if yes break into separate single-purpose instructions. Six \u2014 does it involve data shape changes or migration, if yes confirm before and after data structure explicitly before writing the spec.\n\n15. **CLAUD.MD READ-BACK REQUIRED** \u2014 At the start of every session read claud.md and paste back every rule found. Then identify which rules apply to today's task. If you cannot paste the rules back accurately stop and ask Lauren to re-paste claud.md before proceeding.\n\n16. **MAGNIFICA HUMANITAS DESIGN PRINCIPLES** \u2014 Every feature built must reflect these principles. One \u2014 the app is a tool not an authority. Every AI suggestion is framed as a suggestion never a prescription. Language uses \"here is one way to think about this\" never \"you should\" or \"the optimal schedule is.\" Two \u2014 companions serve real relationships they do not replace them. Every companion orients toward real people, real community, and real pastoral support. Sister Mary never replaces a confessor. Father Gregory never replaces real mentors. Lucy regularly suggests real conversations over app conversations. Three \u2014 AI supports thinking it does not replace it. Ask before suggesting. Boys build their own plans before seeing AI suggestions. Father Gregory asks questions more than he gives answers. Four \u2014 be transparent about what AI is. Companions never make theological claims with personal authority. Prayer texts come from verified Catholic sources only never AI generated. Five \u2014 language of grace not performance. No gamification no streaks no scores that shame. A hard day is never framed as failure. Sick Day Mode is relief not defeat. Six \u2014 subsidiarity. The family governs itself. Lauren is always the authority. The app serves the family's discernment it does not replace it. Seven \u2014 formation in digital wisdom. Father Gregory teaches the boys to think critically about AI. The explicit goal is that JP finishes high school able to plan his day without the app.\n\n17. **ONE FIX PER INSTRUCTION** \u2014 Never bundle multiple fixes into one Agent instruction unless they are in the same file and directly related. Complex multi-file builds must be broken into sequential single-purpose phases with a compile check and report between each phase.\n\n18. **AUGUST 15TH BUILD PLAN IS THE PRIORITY FILTER** \u2014 Between June 1st and August 15th 2026 every build request must be checked against the August 15th build plan before proceeding. If a requested build is not on the must-have or should-have list for the current week flag it to Lauren before starting. New feature ideas go on the post-September list unless they directly enable one of the 14 goals in the August 15th plan. Scope is the first thing to cut not quality.\n\n### Additional sections of claud.md (not numbered as rules but binding context)\n\n- **What this app is** \u2014 Catholic homeschool family management web app, Python on Replit, single-file HTTP server pattern (app.py + render_*.py), no framework.\n- **Stack** \u2014 Python 3.11; no Flask/Django/FastAPI; JSON files only; plain HTML/CSS/JS rendered as strings; Anthropic via urllib (no SDK).\n- **People** \u2014 Lauren (Mom), John (Dad), JP (14, 9th), Joseph (12, 7th), Michael (5, K), James (13 months, excluded from school/gradebook). Title-case names; Lauren/Mom same person; lowercase keys in auth/pins.json and profiles/.\n- **Data file patterns** \u2014 Most data in data/*.json; person keys title-case in progress/chores/events, lowercase in auth/profiles; progress keys `YYYY-MM-DD::Person::task text`; date keys YYYY-MM-DD (most), YYYY-Www (meal_plan), YYYY-MM (cycle).\n- **Route patterns** \u2014 GET routes call render_*.py functions; POST routes chained as `elif path == \"/route\":` in do_POST; JSON POST bodies must be in `_JSON_PATHS` set or the form-parser eats them.\n- **Anchor-tag navigation** \u2014 Plain `<a href>` can't POST; state must travel in query string OR be persisted before click; destination handler must accept those params AND persist them on arrival. Counter-pattern that bit us: FROL wizard landing anchors `/frol-wizard?step=1&mode=structured`. If a button must trigger persistent state, use `<form method=\"POST\">` styled as a link.\n- **AI calls** \u2014 Model `claude-sonnet-4-20250514`, urllib.request (no SDK), API key from app_settings.json, all responses through `_repair_and_parse_json()`.\n- **Change discipline** \u2014 Additive unless told otherwise; don't modify existing behavior beyond task scope; if a task requires editing out-of-scope files, stop and flag; modules under 800 lines where possible; `render_plan_importer.py` is 1,114 lines (JS lives in `static/js/plan_importer_core.js` / `plan_importer_consult.js`).\n- **FROL Wizard form bypass trap** \u2014 `_section_chrome` suppresses \"Save and Continue\" when `_body_has_form` detects a form with `action=\"/frol-wizard\"`. Utility forms posting to other routes (`/frol-set-variant`, `/frol-add-activity`, `/frol-delete-activity`) are safe. When adding new forms to section bodies, check the action \u2014 if it's `/frol-wizard`, use a different route or handle the advance separately.\n- **Current major features** \u2014 `/plan-import` paste\u2192AI\u2192approve\u2192apply with receipt and per-placement undo; six AI companions (Lucy, Lorenzo, Gregory, Monica, Coach, Izzy); liturgical calendar engine with auto-computed Easter and moveable feasts; per-person daily schedule grids; gradebook with assignment analyzer; meal planner with Lorenzo.\n"}}]}, {"role": "tool", "content": [{"type": "text", "text": "File created successfully at: PROJECT_STATE.md"}]}]}

So **meal content has exactly one store**: `data/meal_plan/{Monday}.json`.\n\n`planning_session.json` is **not** a meal store \u2014 it is a wizard progress pointer. The `[MEAL_UPDATE]` handler only *touches* it afterward by calling `advance_planning_session(day, slot)` to move the cursor (`app.py:5908\u20135917`).\n\n---\n\n## Report 2 \u2014 Which store is authoritative?\n\n**There is a single authoritative meal store, and both readers read it. Nothing is merged at render time.**\n\n- **Fridge card** (`/meal-print` \u2192 `render_meal_print_page`, `app.py:1942`) \u2192 `load_meal_plan(week_key)` \u2192 `data/meal_plan/{Monday}.json`.\n- **Lorenzo chat page** \u2192 `_get_current_meal_plan()` (`render_lorenzo.py:66`) \u2192 `load_meal_plan(_planning_week_key())` \u2192 same `data/meal_plan/{Monday}.json`. It even re-derives `_plan_path(start)` purely to report the file's mtime/\"last saved\" to the model.\n\nThe two are deliberately kept in sync by **`_planning_week_key()`** (`render_meals.py:88`): Mon\u2013Thu \u2192 this week's Monday; Fri\u2013Sun \u2192 next Monday \u2014 explicitly so \"Lorenzo and the print card [don't] disagree about which file is the plan.\" \n\n`_get_planning_session_block()` (`render_lorenzo.py:443`) additionally reads `planning_session.json`, but only to tell the model *which slot to work on next* \u2014 that's cursor state, not meal data, and it isn't part of the rendered fridge card.\n\n**Conclusion:** one authoritative store (`data/meal_plan/{Monday}.json`); `planning_session.json` is an orthogonal cursor. No multi-store merge.\n\n---\n\n## Report 3 \u2014 How does the `[MEAL_UPDATE]` tag channel work?\n\nTags are parsed **out of Lorenzo's Anthropic response text**, server-side, inside the `/lorenzo-chat` POST handler \u2014 *after* the model reply is received (`text` at `app.py:5803`). Parser spine, verbatim (`app.py:5806\u20135907`):\n\n```python\n                # \u2500\u2500 Parse [MEAL_UPDATE:Day:slot[|recipe=ID]]meal[/MEAL_UPDATE] and save \u2500\u2500\n                _meal_rx = _re.compile(\n                    r'\\[MEAL_UPDATE:([^:\\]]+):([^|\\]]+)(?:\\|recipe=([^\\]]+))?\\]'\n                    r'([\\s\\S]*?)\\[\\/MEAL_UPDATE\\]',\n                    _re.IGNORECASE\n                )\n                try:\n                    from render_meals import MEAL_SLOT_SET as _DICT_OK_SLOTS\n                except Exception:\n                    _DICT_OK_SLOTS = {\"breakfast\",\"lunch\",\"dinner\",\"dessert\",\"snacks\",\"dad_lunch\"}\n                _meal_updates_found = []\n                for _mm in _meal_rx.finditer(text):\n                    _mday  = _mm.group(1).strip()\n                    _mslot = _mm.group(2).strip().lower()\n                    _mrid  = (_mm.group(3) or \"\").strip()\n                    if _mrid and not _re.fullmatch(r\"[^\\s\\[\\]]+\", _mrid):\n                        print(f\"[lorenzo MEAL_UPDATE] rejected malformed recipe_id: {_mrid!r}\")\n                        _mrid = \"\"\n                    _mmeal = _mm.group(4).strip()\n                    if _mday and _mslot:\n                        _save_ok = False\n                        try:\n                            _wk = _planning_week_key()\n                            _plan = load_meal_plan(_wk)\n                            if _mmeal:\n                                if _mrid and _mslot in _DICT_OK_SLOTS:\n                                    _plan[\"days\"].setdefault(_mday, {})[_mslot] = {\n                                        \"display\":   _mmeal,\n                                        \"recipe_id\": _mrid,\n                                    }\n                                    # [enrichment block elided for length \u2014 app.py:5847\u20135894:\n                                    #  for recipe-linked dinners, fills prep_time/cook_time from\n                                    #  the recipe card, kid 'helpers' via kid_helpers.assign_kid_steps,\n                                    #  and serve_time from the FROL; \"fill blanks only\".]\n                                else:\n                                    _plan[\"days\"].setdefault(_mday, {})[_mslot] = _mmeal\n                            else:\n                                _plan[\"days\"].setdefault(_mday, {}).pop(_mslot, None)\n                            _plan[\"start\"] = _plan.get(\"start\") or _wk\n                            save_meal_plan(_plan)\n                            _save_ok = True\n                        except Exception as _se:\n                            print(f\"[lorenzo MEAL_UPDATE] save failed for {_mday}/{_mslot}: {_se}\")\n                        if _save_ok:\n                            _meal_updates_found.append((_mday, _mslot))\n```\n\n**Where does it write?** To the **`/meal-save-plan` store** \u2014 i.e. the same `data/meal_plan/{Monday}.json`, via the same `save_meal_plan()`. It does **not** write meal data to `planning_session.json` (it only `advance_planning_session()`s the cursor afterward).\n\n**Is it registered in `_JSON_PATHS`?** **No \u2014 and it doesn't need to be, because it never arrives as a POST body.** `_JSON_PATHS = {\"/plan-import-apply\", \"/plan-import-undo-placement\", \"/curriculum-save\", \"/curriculum-minutes\", \"/poetry-passage-save\"}` (`app.py:3453`). The `[MEAL_UPDATE]` text is extracted from the *LLM response*, not from the request body, so the form-parser-consumes-JSON trap (claud.md) cannot apply to it. \n\nWorth noting for completeness: **`/meal-save-plan` is also not in `_JSON_PATHS`, and that is correct** \u2014 it posts `application/x-www-form-urlencoded` fields (`week=\u2026`, `days=<JSON string>`) and `json.loads` the `days` field itself, so the urlencoded parser handles it fine. The claud.md `_JSON_PATHS` gotcha only bites routes that send a **raw JSON request body**; neither save channel does.\n\n---\n\n## Report 4 \u2014 Recommended architecture\n\n**The hypothesis is half-right.** The *store* is already unified \u2014 both `[MEAL_UPDATE]` and `/meal-save-plan` persist to the same `data/meal_plan/{Monday}.json` through `save_meal_plan()`. So the bug is **not** \"two competing stores.\" The real architectural mismatch is in the **save trigger and the confirmation loop**:\n\n1. **The trigger is brittle free-text regex.** `_meal_rx` requires a perfectly-formed `[MEAL_UPDATE:Day:slot]\u2026[/MEAL_UPDATE]`. Any LLM malformation \u2014 missing closing tag, stray bracket/whitespace, the `|recipe=` id failing `[^\\s\\[\\]]+` \u2014 silently yields no match \u2192 **no save**, with no signal back to the model.\n2. **Narration is decoupled from persistence.** Lorenzo's \"I saved it / I couldn't save it\" prose is generated by the model *in the same reply, before the server runs the save*. `_save_ok` captures the *real* result but only feeds `_meal_updates_found` / the false-confirmation guard \u2014 it never corrects the words the model already wrote. Hence \"narrates success or failure inconsistently\": the words and the disk state are produced by two different actors and never reconciled.\n3. **Why the card still renders anyway:** when a tag *is* well-formed, the save genuinely succeeds to the authoritative store, so the fridge card updates \u2014 independent of whatever Lorenzo said.\n\n**Minimum change that would make saves reliable** (recommendation only \u2014 not implemented):\n\n- **Keep the unified store** (`save_meal_plan` / `data/meal_plan/{Monday}.json`) \u2014 don't re-route to `planning_session.json`; that's correct as-is.\n- **Make the confirmation server-driven, not model-driven.** After parsing, the server already knows `_save_ok` and `_meal_updates_found`. The smallest reliable fix is to **stop trusting the model's prose for save status**: strip any model-authored save claims and have the server **append a deterministic confirmation/\u25b2failure line** built from `_save_ok` (e.g. \"Saved Monday dinner \u2713\" / \"Couldn't save Monday dinner \u2014 tag was malformed, try again\"). This closes the narration\u2194persistence gap without changing where data lands.\n- **Optionally tighten the channel** by treating the structured `/meal-save-plan` route as the single write path and having the chat handler *call that same save logic* with parsed args (so there's one persistence code path, one place backups/validation live), rather than a second inline `load\u2192mutate\u2192save` copy. This is a refactor, not required for correctness, but it removes the duplicate save spine.\n\nNet: the fix is **confirmation integrity** (server reports the truth of `_save_ok`), not store migration. The `[MEAL_UPDATE]` channel can stay, but its success/failure messaging must be emitted by the server from the actual save result, not narrated by the model.\n\n---\n\nNo files were modified. I'm skipping the code-review step because this task produced **zero code changes** \u2014 it's a read-only diagnosis deliverable, so there's nothing to review. Tell me which direction you want for the actual fix and I'll scope it as a single change per Rule 17."}]}]}

restore_snapshot | Restore a named snapshot |\n| load_snapshot_data | Load raw snapshot contents |\n| today_iso | Return today's date as ISO string |\n| tomorrow_iso | Return tomorrow's date as ISO these\n\n1. No backslashes inside f-strings\n2. No nested quotes inside f-strings \u2014 use a variable outside the f-string instead\n3. All POST routing uses elif chains \u2014 never if/elif with a missing first if, never nested if blocks for routing\n4. Never put import statements inside if blocks or functions\n5. All file writes use safe_save_json (tmp file + os.replace) \u2014 never open(f, 'w') directly\n6. No walrus operator (`:=`)\n7. Never use `'\\n'` inside a JS string within a Python string literal \u2014 use `'\\\\n'` so the browser receives the escape sequence, not a raw newline\n8. **multipart/form-data parsing** \u2014 when fetch POSTs use FormData the server receives multipart/form-data not urlencoded. The do_POST handler must sniff Content-Type and parse accordingly using cgi.FieldStorage for multipart. If a POST handler receives empty data check the Content-Type first.\n9. **py_compile passes but runtime fails** \u2014 py_compile only validates syntax not runtime correctness. Always run an in-process smoke test after py_compile to catch NameError, missing variable definitions, and import failures.\n10. **test fixtures must never write to live data** \u2014 verification harnesses must always operate on a temp copy of live data files. Never call save_progress, safe_save_json, or any write helper on live data during testing. Always restore from backup after any test that touches data files.\n11. **double-escaping HTML entities** \u2014 never pass a string that is already HTML-escaped through escape() again. If a string contains literal ampersands for display use plain ampersands in the source string and let escape() handle it once. Strings pre-escaped with `&amp;` will render as visible `&amp;` in the browser if escaped again.\n12. **JS newline in Python f-strings applies everywhere** \u2014 rule 7 applies to ALL files containing JS embedded in Python, not just render_frol_wizard.py. This includes render_schedule.py, render_timeblock.py, render_lucy.py, render_lorenzo.py, and any other render file with inline JavaScript.\n\n### Additional rules (13\u201318)\n\n13. **FROL WIZARD NESTED FORM ADDENDUM** \u2014 The _body_has_form check in _section_chrome looks for `action=\"/frol-wizard\"` in the body string. Any form inside a section body posting to /frol-wizard will suppress the Save and Continue button. Variant tab forms posting to /frol-set-variant are safe. Activity builder forms posting to /frol-add-activity are safe. Before adding any form to a section body confirm its action attribute. This is a recurring bug \u2014 document before fixing if it appears again.\n\n14. **PRE-FLIGHT CHECKLIST** \u2014 Before writing any spec answer these questions. One \u2014 how many files does this touch, list them, if unknown that is a diagnosis step first. Two \u2014 does it involve JavaScript inside Python f-strings, if yes flag the backslash-n rule explicitly in the spec. Three \u2014 does it touch form handling, if yes confirm no nested forms posting to /frol-wizard. One \u2014 the app is a tool not an authority. Every AI suggestion is framed as a suggestion never a prescription. Language uses \"here is one way to think about this\" never \"you should\" or \"the optimal schedule is.\" Two \u2014 companions serve real relationships they do not replace them. Every companion orients toward real people, real community, and real pastoral support. Sister Mary never replaces a confessor. Father Gregory never replaces real mentors. Lucy regularly suggests real conversations over app conversations. Three \u2014 AI supports thinking it does not replace it. Ask before suggesting. Boys build their own plans before seeing AI suggestions. Father Gregory asks questions more than he gives answers. Four \u2014 be transparent about what AI is. Companions never make theological claims with personal authority. Prayer texts come from verified Catholic sources only never AI generated. Five \u2014 language of grace not performance. No gamification no streaks no scores that shame. A hard day is never framed as failure. Sick Day Mode is relief not defeat. Six \u2014 subsidiarity. The family governs itself. Lauren is always the authority. The app serves the family's discernment it does not replace it. Seven \u2014 formation in digital wisdom. Father Gregory teaches the boys to think critically about AI. The explicit goal is that JP finishes high school able to plan his day without the app.\n\n17. **ONE FIX PER INSTRUCTION** \u2014 Never bundle multiple fixes into one Agent instruction unless they are in the same file and directly related. Complex multi-file builds must be broken into sequential single-purpose phases with a compile check and report between each phase.\n\n18. **AUGUST 15TH BUILD PLAN IS THE PRIORITY FILTER** \u2014 Between June 1st and August 15th 2026 every build request must be checked against the August 15th build plan before proceeding. So **meal content has exactly one store**: `data/meal_plan/{Monday}.json`.\n\n`planning_session.json` is **not** a meal store \u2014 it is a wizard progress pointer. The `[MEAL_UPDATE]` handler only *touches* it afterward by calling `advance_planning_session(day, slot)` to move the cursor (`app.py:5908\u20135917`).\n\n---\n\n## Report 2 \u2014 Which store is authoritative?\n\n**There is a single authoritative meal store, and both readers read it. Nothing is merged at render time.**\n\n- **Fridge card** (`/meal-print` \u2192 `render_meal_print_page`, `app.py:1942`) \u2192 `load_meal_plan(week_key)` \u2192 `data/meal_plan/{Monday}.json`.\n- **Lorenzo chat page** \u2192 `_get_current_meal_plan()` (`render_lorenzo.py:66`) \u2192 `load_meal_plan(_planning_week_key())` \u2192 same `data/meal_plan/{Monday}.json`. It even re-derives `_plan_path(start)` purely to report the file's mtime/\"last saved\" to the model.\n\nThe two are deliberately kept in sync by **`_planning_week_key()`** (`render_meals.py:88`): Mon\u2013Thu \u2192 this week's Monday; Fri\u2013Sun \u2192 next Monday \u2014 explicitly so \"Lorenzo and the print card [don't] disagree about which file is the plan.\" \n\n`_get_planning_session_block()` (`render_lorenzo.py:443`) additionally reads `planning_session.json`, but only to tell the model *which slot to work on next* \u2014 that's cursor state, not meal data, and it isn't part of the rendered fridge card.\n\n**Conclusion:** one authoritative store (`data/meal_plan/{Monday}.json`); `planning_session.json` is an orthogonal cursor. No multi-store merge.\n\n---\n\n## Report 3 \u2014 How does the `[MEAL_UPDATE]` tag channel work?\n\nTags are parsed **out of Lorenzo's Anthropic response text**, server-side, inside the `/lorenzo-chat` POST handler \u2014 *after* the model reply is received (`text` at `app.py:5803`). Parser spine, verbatim (`app.py:5806\u20135907`):\n\n```python\n                # \u2500\u2500 Parse [MEAL_UPDATE:Day:slot[|recipe=ID]]meal[/MEAL_UPDATE] and save \u2500\u2500\n                _meal_rx = _re.compile(\n                    r'\\[MEAL_UPDATE:([^:\\]]+):([^|\\]]+)(?:\\|recipe=([^\\]]+))?\\]'\n                    r'([\\s\\S]*?)\\[\\/MEAL_UPDATE\\]',\n                    _re.IGNORECASE\n                )\n                try:\n                    from render_meals import MEAL_SLOT_SET as _DICT_OK_SLOTS\n                except Exception:\n                    _DICT_OK_SLOTS = {\"breakfast\",\"lunch\",\"dinner\",\"dessert\",\"snacks\",\"dad_lunch\"}\n                _meal_updates_found = []\n                for _mm in _meal_rx.finditer(text):\n                    _mday  = _mm.group(1).strip()\n                    _mslot = _mm.group(2).strip().lower()\n                    _mrid  = (_mm.group(3) or \"\").strip()\n                    if _mrid and not _re.fullmatch(r\"[^\\s\\[\\]]+\", _mrid):\n                        print(f\"[lorenzo MEAL_UPDATE] rejected malformed recipe_id: {_mrid!r}\")\n                        _mrid = \"\"\n                    _mmeal = _mm.group(4).strip()\n                    if _mday and _mslot:\n                        _save_ok = False\n                        try:\n                            _wk = _planning_week_key()\n                            _plan = load_meal_plan(_wk)\n                            if _mmeal:\n                                if _mrid and _mslot in _DICT_OK_SLOTS:\n                                    _plan[\"days\"].setdefault(_mday, {})[_mslot] = {\n                                        \"display\":   _mmeal,\n                                        \"recipe_id\": _mrid,\n                                    }\n                                    # [enrichment block elided for length \u2014 app.py:5847\u20135894:\n                                    #  for recipe-linked dinners, fills prep_time/cook_time from\n                                    #  the recipe card, kid 'helpers' via kid_helpers.assign_kid_steps,\n                                    #  and serve_time from the FROL; \"fill blanks only\".]\n                                else:\n                                    _plan[\"days\"].setdefault(_mday, {})[_mslot] = _mmeal\n                            else:\n                                _plan[\"days\"].setdefault(_mday, {}).pop(_mslot, None)\n                            _plan[\"start\"] = _plan.get(\"start\") or _wk\n                            save_meal_plan(_plan)\n                            _save_ok = True\n                        except Exception as _se:\n                            print(f\"[lorenzo MEAL_UPDATE] save failed for {_mday}/{_mslot}: {_se}\")\n                        if _save_ok:\n                            _meal_updates_found.append((_mday, _mslot))\n```\n\n**Where does it write?** To the **`/meal-save-plan` store** \u2014 i.e. the same `data/meal_plan/{Monday}.json`, via the same `save_meal_plan()`. It does **not** write meal data to `planning_session.json` (it only `advance_planning_session()`s the cursor afterward).\n\n**Is it registered in `_JSON_PATHS`?** **No \u2014 and it doesn't need to be, because it never arrives as a POST body.** `_JSON_PATHS = {\"/plan-import-apply\", \"/plan-import-undo-placement\", \"/curriculum-save\", \"/curriculum-minutes\", \"/poetry-passage-save\"}` (`app.py:3453`). The `[MEAL_UPDATE]` text is extracted from the *LLM response*, not from the request body, so the form-parser-consumes-JSON trap (claud.md) cannot apply to it. \n\nWorth noting for completeness: **`/meal-save-plan` is also not in `_JSON_PATHS`, and that is correct** \u2014 it posts `application/x-www-form-urlencoded` fields (`week=\u2026`, `days=<JSON string>`) and `json.loads` the `days` field itself, so the urlencoded parser handles it fine. The claud.md `_JSON_PATHS` gotcha only bites routes that send a **raw JSON request body**; neither save channel does.\n\n---\n\n## Report 4 \u2014 Recommended architecture\n\n**The hypothesis is half-right.** The *store* is already unified \u2014 both `[MEAL_UPDATE]` and `/meal-save-plan` persist to the same `data/meal_plan/{Monday}.json` through `save_meal_plan()`. So the bug is **not** \"two competing stores.\" The real architectural mismatch is in the **save trigger and the confirmation loop**:\n\n1. **The trigger is brittle free-text regex.** `_meal_rx` requires a perfectly-formed `[MEAL_UPDATE:Day:slot]\u2026[/MEAL_UPDATE]`. Any LLM malformation \u2014 missing closing tag, stray bracket/whitespace, the `|recipe=` id failing `[^\\s\\[\\]]+` \u2014 silently yields no match \u2192 **no save**, with no signal back to the model.\n2. **Narration is decoupled from persistence.** Lorenzo's \"I saved it / I couldn't save it\" prose is generated by the model *in the same reply, before the server runs the save*. `_save_ok` captures the *real* result but only feeds `_meal_updates_found` / the false-confirmation guard \u2014 it never corrects the words the model already wrote. Hence \"narrates success or failure inconsistently\": the words and the disk state are produced by two different actors and never reconciled.\n3. **Why the card still renders anyway:** when a tag *is* well-formed, the save genuinely succeeds to the authoritative store, so the fridge card updates \u2014 independent of whatever Lorenzo said.\n\n**Minimum change that would make saves reliable** (recommendation only \u2014 not implemented):\n\n- **Keep the unified store** (`save_meal_plan` / `data/meal_plan/{Monday}.json`) \u2014 don't re-route to `planning_session.json`; that's correct as-is.\n- **Make the confirmation server-driven, not model-driven.** After parsing, the server already knows `_save_ok` and `_meal_updates_found`. The smallest reliable fix is to **stop trusting the model's prose for save status**: strip any model-authored save claims and have the server **append a deterministic confirmation/\u25b2failure line** built from `_save_ok` (e.g. \"Saved Monday dinner \u2713\" / \"Couldn't save Monday dinner \u2014 tag was malformed, try again\"). This closes the narration\u2194persistence gap without changing where data lands.\n- **Optionally tighten the channel** by treating the structured `/meal-save-plan` route as the single write path and having the chat handler *call that same save logic* with parsed args (so there's one persistence code path, one place backups/validation live), rather than a second inline `load\u2192mutate\u2192save` copy. This is a refactor, not required for correctness, but it removes the duplicate save spine.\n\nNet: the fix is **confirmation integrity** (server reports the truth of `_save_ok`), not store migration. The `[MEAL_UPDATE]` channel can stay, but its success/failure messaging must be emitted by the server from the actual save result, not narrated by the model.\n\n---\n\nNo files were modified. I'm skipping the code-review step because this task produced **zero code changes** \u2014 it's a read-only diagnosis deliverable, so there's nothing to review. Tell me which direction you want for the actual fix and I'll scope it as a single change per Rule 17."}]}]}
